The case is sent on remand to the High Court Division for fresh disposal of the appeal by a different Bench.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"><strong><em>The State Vs. Abdul Khaleque alias Abdul Khaleq Howlader, 17BLD(AD)188</em></strong></p><p style="text-align: justify;"><strong> </strong></p><p style="text-align: justify;"><strong>Section—410</strong></p><p style="text-align: justify;">Criminal prosecution involves many participants in a complicated sequences of steps, such as the Judges, the lawyers, investigating agency, witnesses of the public, expert witnesses etc. which involves public expense, time etc. If a superior Court disposes a criminal matter, more particularly a criminal appeal of such a great importance in a light hearted manner without any application of judicial mind then that will have a demoralizing effect on the subordinate judiciary in disposing criminal justice in Bangladesh.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"><strong><em>The State Vs Giasuddin and others,18BLD(AD)254</em></strong></p><p style="text-align: justify;"><strong>Ref:</strong> 1953 PLD(FC)317; PLD 1966 (Labore) 8; 39 DLR(AD) 117—Cited</p><p style="text-align: justify;"><strong> </strong></p><p style="text-align: justify;"><strong>Section—417</strong></p><p style="text-align: justify;"><strong>Appeal against acquittal</strong></p><p style="text-align: justify;">As a matter of practice the High Court Division normally grants bail to the persons who are acquitted after a full-fledged trial when the State prefers an appeal against the order of acquittal. The normal order upon admitting the Government appeal is to direct the Deputy Commissioner concerned to take the acquitted persons into custody and release them on bail to the satisfaction of the Deputy Commissioner.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"><strong><em>Abdul Hafez Howlader alias Habibur Rahman and others Vs. The State, 19 BLD (AD)1</em></strong></p><p style="text-align: justify;"><strong> </strong></p><p style="text-align: justify;"><strong>Sections—417A and 404</strong></p><p style="text-align: justify;">Sentence can be enhanced by the High Court Division after giving a reasonable opportunity of showing cause against such enhancement when an appeal is filed under section 417A of the Code by a complainant against any sentence on the ground of its inadequacy. In view of the provisions of section 404 of the Code no appeal shall lie from any judgment or order of criminal court except as provided by the Code. So, except under the provisions of section 417A of the Code, there is no other provisions for filing any appeal for enhancement of any sentence.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"><strong><em>Moktar Ali Bepari Vs. The State and another, 19BLD(HCD)259</em></strong></p><p style="text-align: justify;"><strong> </strong></p><p style="text-align: justify;"><strong>Section—422</strong></p><p style="text-align: justify;"><strong>Notice of appeal</strong></p><p style="text-align: justify;">It provides that after a criminal appeal against an order of conviction and sentence is admitted for hearing, the appellate Court is required to give notice to the appellant or to his lawyer as well as to the State mentioning the time and place of hearing of the appeal. It does not contemplate issuance of any notice to the complainant, because after the complaint case has ended in conviction, the State comes to the picture as it is the duty of the State to execute the verdict of conviction and sentence imposed upon the accused. Thus a complainant cannot claim any right of audience in an appeal in which the accused has been convicted and sentenced by the trial Court on the basis of a complaint made by a private individual.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"><strong><em>Md. Kamal Miah alias Nasim Vs. The State and another, 18BLD(HCD)187</em></strong></p><p style="text-align: justify;"><strong>Ref:</strong> AIR 1 960(Andra Prodesh)311-relied</p><p style="text-align: justify;"><strong> </strong></p><p style="text-align: justify;"><strong>Section—417(1)</strong></p><p style="text-align: justify;"><strong>Acquittal</strong></p><p style="text-align: justify;">Order of acquittal cannot be interfered by the appellate court unless it is found that the said order is manifestly perverse. A finding cannot be said to be perverse if it is against weight of evidence.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"><strong><em>The State Vs Mrs. Shamima Arshad, 20BLD(HCD)315</em></strong></p><p style="text-align: justify;"><strong>Ref:</strong> A1R1966 Cal 31; 9DLR(1957) WP) 13; 37DLR(AD) 167—Cited</p><p style="text-align: justify;"><strong> </strong></p><p style="text-align: justify;"><strong>Sections—423 and 408</strong></p><p style="text-align: justify;">In an appeal from a conviction, sentence may be reduced by an appellate Court but sentence cannot be enhanced. From subsection (1)(bb) of section 423 it is also clear that sentence can be enhanced only in an appeal for enhancement of sentence and that can be done after giving the accused an opportunity of showing cause against such enhancement.</p><p style="text-align: justify;">In the instant appeal, the appellate Court had no power to enhance the sentence of the appellants who filed the appeal under section 408 of the Code against their conviction by the trial court. Obviously, the enhancement of sentence of the appellants was illegal and without jurisdiction.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"><strong><em>Moktar Ali Bepari Vs. The State and another, 19BLD(HCD)259</em></strong></p><p style="text-align: justify;"><strong> </strong></p><p style="text-align: justify;"><strong>Section—423(1)(bb)</strong></p><p style="text-align: justify;">In view of the provision of section 423(1)(bb) of the Code in an appeal for enhancement of sentence, the appellate Court. may enhance the sentence but such enhancement cannot be made unless the accused is given an opportunity of showing cause against such enhancement. In the instant case the appeal was not an appeal for enhancement of sentence. It was an appeal under section 408 of the Code of Criminal Procedure against the judgment and order of conviction and sentence passed by the trial Court. So, instant appeal the appellate Court has no power to impose the sentence of fine.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"><strong><em>Mizanur Rzhman Vs. Mst. Surma Khatun, 18BLD(HCD)512</em></strong></p><p style="text-align: justify;"><strong>Ref:</strong> 1BLD(1981)(HCD)165—Cited</p><p style="text-align: justify;"><strong> </strong></p><p style="text-align: justify;"><strong>Section—426</strong></p><p style="text-align: justify;"><strong>Bail in a pending appeal involving murder charge</strong></p><p style="text-align: justify;">The accused petitioner and others were convicted under section 302/34 of the Penal Code and sentenced to imprisonment for life solely on the basis of the ex-culpatory confessional statements of the co-accused. The petitioner has already suffered more than two and half years of his sentence—There is no chance of hearing of the appeal in the near future—In view of the above facts and circumstances the accused petitioner is enlarged on bail till disposal of the appeal.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"><strong><em>Md. Ayub Ali Vs. The State, 14BLD(HCD)501</em></strong></p><p style="text-align: justify;"><strong> </strong></p><p style="text-align: justify;"><strong>Section—426</strong></p><p style="text-align: justify;"><strong>Bail in a short period of sentence</strong></p><p style="text-align: justify;">In an appeal against a short sentence bail should be ordinarily granted in the exercise of a proper discretion because usually it takes time to hear the appeal and with the passage of the period of sentence the appeal becomes intructuous.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"><strong><em>Alal Uddin Vs The State, 19BLD(AD)202</em></strong></p><p style="text-align: justify;"><strong>Ref:</strong> 1 1BLD(AD)9 6—Cited</p><p style="text-align: justify;"><strong><span style="background: yellow;"> </span></strong></p><p style="text-align: justify;"><strong><span style="background: transparent none repeat scroll 0% 0%;">Section—426</span></strong></p><p style="text-align: justify;"><span style="background-color: #ffffff;"><span style="background-image: none; background-repeat: repeat; background-attachment: scroll; background-position: 0% 0%; background-clip: border-box; background-origin: padding-box; background-size: auto auto;">The appellants and six others were put on trial before an Additional Sessions Judge, Barisal to answer charges under section 302/34 of the Penal Code and after a fuilfledged trial the accused persons were acquitted. Against this order of acquittal the State filed an appeal before the High Court Division. The appellant’s prayer for bail was refused by the High Court Division.</span></span></p><p style="text-align: justify;"><span style="background-color: #ffffff;"><span style="background-image: none; background-repeat: repeat; background-attachment: scroll; background-position: 0% 0%; background-clip: border-box; background-origin: padding-box; background-size: auto auto;">The Appellate Division held that in normal circumstances bail is granted in such cases as because the accused have already satisfied the competent court that there are no reasonable grounds for believing that they have committed the alleged offence. It is also the normal practice of the High Court Division to grant bail in such circumstances. It has been further held that as a measure of punishment bail should not be refused in a case when an order of acquittal has been passed. Bail is granted to the appellants.</span></span></p><p style="text-align: justify;"><span style="background-color: #ffffff;"><strong><em><span style="background-image: none; background-repeat: repeat; background-attachment: scroll; background-position: 0% 0%; background-clip: border-box; background-origin: padding-box; background-size: auto auto;">Abdul Hafiz Howlader </span><span style="background-image: none; background-repeat: repeat; background-attachment: scroll; background-position: 0% 0%; background-clip: border-box; background-origin: padding-box; background-size: auto auto;">alias Habibur Rahman and others Vs. The State, 15BLD (AD)144</span></em></strong></span></p><p style="text-align: justify;"><strong> </strong></p><p style="text-align: justify;"><strong>Section—426(2)</strong></p><p style="text-align: justify;">In appeals involving short term of imprisonment the appellate Court should either dispose of the appeal expeditiously or consider the release of the appellant on bail. It is not necessary for the appellate Court to write a long judgment for the purpose of disposal of the bail petition.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"><strong><em>Mahbub and others Vs. The State, 14 BLD (AD)184</em></strong></p><p style="text-align: justify;"><strong> </strong></p><p style="text-align: justify;"><strong>Section-426(2A)</strong></p><p style="text-align: justify;">Section 426, sub-section 2A Cr.P.C is the section which entitles lower Court to grant bail to a convict for a limited period after conviction in order to enable him to prefer an appeal.</p><p style="margin-bottom: 12.0pt;"><strong><em>Shaheb Ali Vs. The State, 13BLD (HCD) 445</em></strong></p><p style="text-align: justify;"><strong> </strong></p><p style="text-align: justify;"><strong>Section—426(2B)</strong></p><p style="text-align: justify;">Bail under section 426(2A) Cr.P.C may be granted both by the trial Court and by the appellate Court. But the conviction in such a case must not carry beyond one year. But the very language of the section shows that the power to grant bail under section 426(2A) Cr.P.C. is not available either to the trial Court or to the appellate Court when the conviction carries senterfce of imprisonment of more than one year.</p><p style="text-align: justify;">Under section 426(2B) Cr.P.C High Court Division may grant bail to the convict or suspend the sentence after disposal of the appeal or revision irrespective of the period of sentence imposed, if only it is satisfactorily proved that leave to appeal has been granted by the Appellate Division. The legislature intended that the lower court under section 426 (2B) Cr.P.C could be exercised only when the sentence did not exceed one year.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"><strong><em>Shaheb Ali Vs The State, 13BLD(FICD) 445</em></strong></p><p style="text-align: justify;"><strong>Ref:</strong> 43DLR(AD) 120—Cited</p><p style="text-align: justify;"><strong> </strong></p><p style="text-align: justify;"><strong>Sections— 435, 338 and 439A</strong></p><p style="text-align: justify;">Legislature has consciously kept section 438 alive even the Sessions Judges have been invested with the powers under section 439A to make final orders enabling the litigants to chose the forum as to whether he would resort to the fotum provided under section 438 or under section 439A with the risk of finality of the order that may be passed in relation to him only.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"><strong><em>Abdul Ahad @ Md Abdul Ahad Vs The State, 20BLD(HCD)372</em></strong></p><p style="text-align: justify;"><strong> </strong></p><p style="text-align: justify;"><strong>Section—436</strong></p><p style="text-align: justify;"><strong>Notice to the accused</strong></p><p style="text-align: justify;">Notice to the accused person is not necessary in a revision u/s 436 Cr.P.C. directed against the dismissal of a complaint. The Court is not required to issue a notice to the accused persons at the preliminary stage of taking cognizance by issuing processes.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"><strong><em>Sirajuddowla and others Vs. The State and another, 15BLD(HCD)607</em></strong></p><p style="text-align: justify;"><strong>Ref:</strong> A.I.R.1927 (Madras) 19 (FB); 1971 Supreme Court Cases (Cr1) 446; A.I.R. 1959 (SC) 144—Cited</p><p style="text-align: justify;"><strong> </strong></p><p style="text-align: justify;"><strong>Section—438</strong></p><p style="text-align: justify;">Sessions Judges have been given revisional powers to make final orders but simultaneously their powers of to make recommendation to the High Court Division for orders under section 438 have also been kept intact.</p><p style="text-align: justify;">The intention of the legislature is clear and obvious. It is that a litigant has been given option to choose the forum, whether he would avail the powers of the Sessions Judge either under section 438 or under Section 439A of the Code. When a litigant resorts to section 438 of the Code of Criminal Procedure, Sessions Judges must read section 435 of the said Code together, because section 438 is not independent of section 435.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"><strong><em>AbdulAhad @ MdAbdulAhad Vs The State, 20BLD(HCD)372</em></strong></p><p style="text-align: justify;"><strong> </strong></p><p style="text-align: justify;"><strong>Section—439</strong></p><p style="text-align: justify;">Under section 439 Cr.P.C. the High Court Division can suo motu call for the records and correct any error in the order of the Court below. Order showing the accused arrested and allowing remand is illegal and not sustainable and as such liable to be set aside.</p><p style="margin-bottom: 12.0pt;"><strong><em>Aftabur Rahrnan alias Zangi Vs. The State, 13BLD(HCD)547</em></strong></p><p style="text-align: justify;"><strong>Ref:</strong> 34 DLR(AD) 222; (1969) Pakistan Criminal Law Journal 873; AIR 1935 Lahore 230; 1992 Pakistan Criminal Law Journal 985—Cited</p><p style="text-align: justify;"><strong> </strong></p><p style="text-align: justify;"><strong>Section—439</strong></p><p style="text-align: justify;">When the appellate Court and the High Court Division, upon a view of the rest of the evidence and circumstances which is not unreasonable or perverse, refused to believe the prosecution case, it is settled law that this Court, merely because a different view is possible on the evidence, does not interfere with an order of acquittal.</p><p style="text-align: justify;">Unless it is possible to demonstrate with certainty that none of the grounds upon which the learned Judges have purported to acquit is at all supportable, this Court will be reluctant to interfere, even though upon the evidence on the record and the facts and circumstances of the case this Court might well have come to a different conclusion if it was trying the case.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"><strong><em>Md. Abdul Hamid Mollah Vs. Ali Mollah and another, 13BLD(AD)127</em></strong></p><p style="text-align: justify;"><strong>Ref:</strong> Siraj Din Vs Kala, 16DLR (SC)94— Cited</p><p style="text-align: justify;"><strong> </strong></p><p style="text-align: justify;"><strong>Section—439</strong></p><p style="text-align: justify;">Under section 439 of the Code of Criminal Procedure the High Court Division may also suo motu call for the record of the Courts subordinate to it and set aside any order passed by such Courts in any legal proceeding which has caused miscarriage of justice.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"><strong><em>Md. Reazuddin Ahmed Vs The State and another, 17BLD(AD)123</em></strong></p><p style="text-align: justify;"><strong> </strong></p><p style="text-align: justify;"><strong>Section—439</strong></p><p style="text-align: justify;">The High Court Division under section 439 of the Code having supervisory jurisdiction can scrutinise and go into facts of a case to examine the propriety of the orders passed under section 265C or 265D of the Code.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"><strong><em>Mrs. Jobaida Rashid Vs The State, 17BLD (HCD)352</em></strong></p><p style="text-align: justify;"><strong> </strong></p><p style="text-align: justify;"><strong>Section—439A</strong></p><p style="text-align: justify;">The learned Sessions Judge can not pass any direction for framing charge under a particular Section of the Penal Code. Considering the case of the respective parties, the learned Sessions Judge may direct for further enquiry but he can not form his own opinion in such a revisional application and direct the trial Court to frame charge under a particular section of the Penal Code. If, during trial, it transpires that charge ought to have been framed under a higher Section of the Penal Code or a change in the charge is necessary, then the trial Court may take any step for framing fresh charge and proceed with the trial.</p><p style="text-align: justify;">Section 242 of the Code of Criminal Procedure has given wide power to the trial Court to frame a charge under a particular section of the Penal Code which can not be interfered with by the revisional Court by way of giving direction for altering the charge or framing the charge.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"><strong><em>Shariful Islam Vs. Md. Billal Hossain and The State, 13BLD(HCD)392</em></strong></p><p style="text-align: justify;"><strong> </strong></p><p style="text-align: justify;"><strong>Section-439A</strong></p><p style="text-align: justify;">While deciding a revisional application a Sessions Judge or an Additional Sessions Judge can deal with questions of facts of a case as much as an Appellate Court and on consideration of the evidence on record he may reverse the judgment of the learned Magistrate. But in reversing such a judgment he is required to advert to the reasons assigned by and the findings arrived at by the Magistrate.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"><strong><em>Shamsuddin alias Shamsuddoha Vs. Amjad A14 15BLD(HCD) 197</em></strong></p><p style="text-align: justify;"><strong>Ref:</strong> 44 DLR (AD) 56—Cited</p><p style="text-align: justify;"><strong> </strong></p><p style="text-align: justify;"><strong>Sections—439 A and 561 A</strong></p><p style="text-align: justify;">Remedy under Section 561A Cr.P.C. is available to a party in an appropriate case even after the Sessions Judge exercised his power under Section 439A Cr.P.C.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"><strong><em>Md. Soleman Vs. A. Barek Khalifa and Others, 15BLD(HCD) 198</em></strong></p><p style="text-align: justify;"><strong>Ref:</strong> 4 BLD (AD) 165; 26 DLR 17; 27 DLR 260; 20 DLR (DACCA) 367; PLD 1968 (Peshwar) 214; 25 Cr1 L. J. 1161 (Rangoon); 50 Cr1. L. J. 967 (All); 32 Cr1. L.J. 1237 (Cal); A.I.R. 1947 (Lahore) 227—Cited</p><p style="text-align: justify;"><strong> </strong></p><p style="text-align: justify;"><strong>Sections—439 (4) and 561A</strong></p><p style="text-align: justify;">The “total bar “ contemplated in section 439(4) Cr.P.C. is only against further revision and not against the inherent jurisdiction of the High Court Division. The High Court Division, on the one hand, willfully disregarded the decisions of the Appellate Division, and on the other hand, flouted Article 111 of the Constitution which is strongly disapproved.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"><strong><em>Md. Sher Ali and others Vs The State and another, 14BLD(AD)84</em></strong></p><p style="text-align: justify;"><strong> </strong></p><p style="text-align: justify;"><strong>Section—439</strong></p><p style="text-align: justify;"><strong>Anti-Corruption Act, 1957 (XXVI of 1957)</strong></p><p style="text-align: justify;"><strong>Sections—3,4 and 5</strong></p><p style="text-align: justify;">Provision of the Act can be resorted to for enquire into or for investigation of pecuniary resources or property of any person either he is a public servant or any other else or in other words ‘an ordinary citizen’ and as such the provisions of the Act is not applicable in the case of petitioner, who is ‘an ordinary citizen’ is not correct.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"><strong><em>A KM Muhituddin Vs The State, 19BLD (HCD)455</em></strong></p><p style="text-align: justify;"><strong> </strong></p><p style="text-align: justify;"><strong>Sections—439A and 561A</strong></p><p style="text-align: justify;">In view of the absolute bar made in section 439(4), the High Court Division cannot entertain any proceeding against an order passed by the Sessions Judge under section 439A. The general provision under Section 561A cannot be invoked to circumvent the absolute bar under section 439(4) and to make the same nugatory.</p><p style="text-align: justify;">Sessions Judge exercising power under section 439A Cr.P.C. having been equated with the High Court Division exercising power under Section 439 Cr.P.C., the order passed by the Sessions Judge cannot be interfered with by the High Court Division by resorting to section 561A of the Code as the order so passed by the Sessions Judge would be deemed to be an order passed by the High Court Division and as such the High Court Division is not permitted to review its own order or Judgment by having recourse to section 561A Cr.P.C. In such a case the aggrieved party may move the Appellate Division directly against the order of the Sessions Judge.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"><strong><em>Mafizuddin and Others Vs. Alauddin and another, 14BLD(HCD)45</em></strong></p><p style="text-align: justify;"><strong> </strong></p><p style="text-align: justify;"><strong>Section—439(2)</strong></p><p style="text-align: justify;">Awarding sentence of fine along with imprisonment for life can not be said to be illegal in view of the section 409 of the Penal Code</p><p style="text-align: justify;">If the sentence of fine is to be enhanced then a Rule should be issued upon the appellant to show cause why the sentence to pay a fine imposed upon him under the impugned judgment should not be enhanced.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"><strong><em>A.M.A. Wazedul Islam Vs. The State 13BLD(HCD)296</em></strong></p><p style="text-align: justify;"><strong> </strong></p><p style="text-align: justify;"><strong>Section—476</strong></p><p style="text-align: justify;">The Court issued a suo motu Rule under section 476 of the Code upon delinquent Abdul Majid to show cause as to why an inquiry should not be made as to whether he gave false evidence as PW.2 on 19.4.1992 before Bar Council Tribunal No.1 in a complaint case and there by conmitted an offence punishable under section 193 of the Penal Code.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"><strong><em>Abdul Hamid Advocate Vs. Bangladesh Bar Council, 17BLD(HCD)547</em></strong></p><p style="text-align: justify;"><strong> </strong></p><p style="text-align: justify;"><strong>Section—476</strong></p><p style="text-align: justify;">In view of the provisions of section 476 Cr.P.C a Court cannot proceed directly against any person for giving false evidence or fabricating evidence. The Court cannot also impose any fine upon any witness or direct him to pay any compensation to the accused. A Tribunal constituted under section 26 of the Special Powers Act is required to follow the provisions of section 476 Cr. P.C if it wants to proceed against any witness for commission of an offence under section 193 of the Penal Code.</p><p style="margin-bottom: 12.0pt;"><strong><em>Md. Idris Miah Vs. The State, 18BLD (HCD)288</em></strong></p><p style="margin-bottom: 12.0pt;"><strong> </strong></p><p style="margin-bottom: 12.0pt;"><strong>Section—476B</strong></p><p style="text-align: justify;">Any person on whose application any Civil, Revenue or Criminal Court has refused to make a complaint under section. 476 or section 476A, or against whom such a complaint has been made may, appeal to the Court to which such former Court is subordinate within the meaning of section 195, subsection (3), and the superior Court may thereupon, after notice to the parties concerned direct the withdrawal of the complaint or as the case may be, itself make the complaint which the subordinate Court. might have made under section 476, and if it makes such complaint the provisions of that section shall apply accordingly.”</p><p style="text-align: justify;">The language of the above provision is clear and unambiguous. All that the appellate court can do is to direct the withdrawal of the complaint if made by the trial court or itself to make the complaint which might have been made by the subordinate Court. In case of making complaint the appellate court is to follow the provision of section 476. The authority of the appellate Court is thus clearly pronounced and it can not go beyond it. Sending a case on remand by the appellate court amounts to acting beyond jurisdiction.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"><strong><em>Khizir Hayat Khan Eusuf Zai Vs Major (Rtd) Md. Muqtadir Ali &amp; ors, 20BLD (AD)46</em></strong></p><p style="text-align: justify;"><strong> </strong></p><p style="text-align: justify;"><strong>Section—488</strong></p><p style="text-align: justify;"><strong>Family Courts Ordinance, 1985 (XVIII of 1985)</strong></p><p style="text-align: justify;">Under section 5 of the Family Courts Ordinance the Family Court has exclusive jurisdiction to try any suit for maintenance. An application for maintenance under section 488 of the Code of Criminal Procedure not being a suit, is not within the exclusive jurisdiction of the Family Court. The provisions of the Family Courts Ordinance have not therefore taken away power of the Magistrate to order for maintenance under section 488 of the Code of Criminal Procedure.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"><strong><em>Zinnatan Nessa Vs. Md. Kaloo Mia, 15 BLD(HCD)545</em></strong></p><p style="text-align: justify;"><strong>Ref:</strong> 14 BLD 467:47 DLR 18—Cited</p><p style="text-align: justify;"><strong> </strong></p><p style="text-align: justify;"><strong>Section—488</strong></p><p style="text-align: justify;"><strong>Family Courts Ordinance, 1985(VIII of 1985)</strong></p><p style="text-align: justify;">The provisions of the Family Courts Ordinance, 1985 have not ousted the jurisdiction of a Magistrate to order for maintenance to wife and children under section 488 Cr.P.C.</p><p style="text-align: justify;">The provisions of the Family Courts Ordinancè, 1985 have not ousted the jurisdiction of a Magistrate to order for maintenance to wife and children under section 488 Cr.P.C.</p><p style="text-align: justify;">The provisions of the Family Courts Ordinance, 1985 are applicable not only to the Muslim community but also to other communities which constitute the populace of Bangladesh.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"><strong><em>Abdul Khaleque Vs. Selina Begum and another, 14BLD(HCD)467</em></strong></p><p style="text-align: justify;"><strong> </strong></p><p style="text-align: justify;"><strong>Section—488</strong></p><p style="text-align: justify;">A proceeding under section 488 of the Code of Criminal Procedure is quasi-criminal and quasi-civil in nature, which gives certain specified powers to the Magistrate to grant maintenance to wives and children who are unable to maintain themselves. The combined effect of the provisions of sections 3, 4, 5 and 27 of the Family Courts Ordinance, 1985 is that the jurisdiction of the Magistrates in dealing with matters contained in section 488 of the Code is clearly ousted after coming into operation of the Family Court Ordinance. 1985.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"><strong><em>Pachan Rissi Das Vs. Khuku Rani Dasi, 17BLD(HCD)563</em></strong></p><p style="text-align: justify;"><strong>Ref:</strong> AIR 1961(SC)1152; 14BLD415; 14 BLD 413; 47 DLR18; 2IDLR (1969)123; PLD 1984(SC)95 :PLD 1 984(SC)95; PLD 1971 (Karachi) 887; 42 DLR450 ; PLD 1969 (SC) 187—Cited</p><p style="text-align: justify;"><strong> </strong></p><p style="text-align: justify;"><strong>Section—491</strong></p><p style="text-align: justify;">In a habeas corpus proceeding under section 491 Cr.P.C. the question of entire detention of the detenu is before the Court. The High Court Division is competent not only in declaring the detention of the detenu illegal but also competent in declaring the proceedings upon which the detenu was held in detention to be illegal and void.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"><strong><em>The State Vs. Deputy Commissioner, Satkhira, and others, 14BLD(JICD)266</em></strong></p><p style="text-align: justify;"><strong> </strong></p><p style="text-align: justify;"><strong>Section—491</strong></p><p style="text-align: justify;">The High Court Division after having found the victim girl to be a minor was not all justified in refusing to give her to the lawful custody of her father. The refusal of the minor to go with her father is not at all a material consideration in respect of her custody. Father being the best well-wisher of his minor daughter is entitled to her custody and it is in her own interest that the minor should be given to her fathers custody. Further, the minor girl is an unfortunate victim of an offence</p><p style="text-align: justify;">of abduction and it is not understood as to why she should be detained in jail till the disposal of the criminal case as well as till she attains the age of 18 years.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"><strong><em>Sree Mongal Chandra Nandi Vs Bangladesh and others, 17BLD(AD)33</em></strong></p><p style="text-align: justify;"><strong>Ref:</strong> Criminal Petition For Leave To Appeal No. 101 of 1996—Unreported.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"><strong> </strong></p><p style="text-align: justify;"><strong>Section—491</strong></p><p style="text-align: justify;">From the S.S.C Certificate produced by the father of the victim girl it is found that she is around 18 years of age. She is not an accused in the case. In such circumstances, judicial custody of the victim girl was not found be proper.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"><strong><em>Sree Tarapada Sarker Vs The State and ors, 17BLD(HCD)379</em></strong></p><p style="text-align: justify;"><strong>Ref:</strong> 16 BLD (1996) (AD) 124; 48 DLR (AD) 67:1996 BLT(AD)112; 17BLD (1997) (AD) 33: 1997 BLT (AD)1; 15DLR148; 35 DLR315; 9BLD(1989) 469—Cited</p><p style="text-align: justify;"><strong> </strong></p><p style="text-align: justify;"><strong>Section—491</strong></p><p style="text-align: justify;"><strong>Custody of victim girl</strong></p><p style="text-align: justify;">Prima facie it appears that the victim girl is a minor (final determination will be made at the trial) and she is a victim of an alleged offence committed by the accused. She was put to judicial custody by the Magistrate in April, 1997 when she was produced before him. Since than she has been staying in a prison house except for a few days when she came out therefrom on getting ad-interim bail from the High Court Division. It is entirely unacceptable that a young girl who is an innocent victim of the alleged offence should remain in an wholesome atmosphere of a Jail for an indefinite period. The young girl cannot be allowed to walk away from the prison house of her own, because she had no independent place to stay. The welfare of the girl, should be deciding factor in such a situation. The appellant produced a certificate from the school where the girl was reading which corroborates the statements of the appellant that his daughter was a minor at the relevant time. The radiologist’s opinion also supports the appellants case.</p><p style="text-align: justify;">From the above facts and circumstances and having considered all aspects of the matter it will be fit and proper and in the best interest of the girl if she is released from custody and given to the care of her father.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"><strong><em>Bashu Deb Chatterjee Vs Umme Salma and another, 19BLD(AD)137</em></strong></p><p style="text-align: justify;"><strong> </strong></p><p style="text-align: justify;"><strong>Section—491(3)</strong></p><p style="text-align: justify;">The Supreme Court being the guardian of the Constitution and protector of the liberty of the citizens, Sub-section 3 of Section 491 Cr.P.C. does not debar the High Court Division from examining the case of a detenu to satisfy itself if the detenu is illegally or improperly detained or that he is being detained without any lawful authority for non-compliance of any mandatory provision of law or for colourable exercise of powers and to declare his detention illegal if materials on record do not justify it.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"><strong><em>Mallick Tarikul Islam Vs. The Secretary, Ministry of Home Affairs and others, 14BLD (HCD)156</em></strong></p><p style="text-align: justify;"><strong> </strong></p><p style="text-align: justify;"><strong>Section—494</strong></p><p style="text-align: justify;"><strong>Withdrawal from prosecution</strong></p><p style="text-align: justify;">The consent mentioned in section 494 of the Code is not to be given mechanically. The court is to exercise its function judicially before giving such consent which implies that the court will have to examine the materials on which the Government decides withdraw of a case.</p><p style="text-align: justify;">In the instant case no reason/ground has been assigned for the withdrawal of the case and there is no indication that materials were considered before taking the decision and the Divisional Special Judge committed illegality in allowing withdrawal under the circumstances. The High Court Division also failed to appreciate the legal aspect of the matter and wrongly refused to interfere in the matter and thereby committed illegality.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"><strong><em>Sreemati Prativa Rani Dey(Tirtha) Vs Dr. Mohammad Yousuf, Medical Officer, Emergency Department, Chittagong Medical College Hospital and others, 20BLD(AD)54</em></strong></p><p style="text-align: justify;"><strong> </strong></p><p style="text-align: justify;"><strong>Section—494</strong></p><p style="text-align: justify;"><strong>Discretion of Court-withdraw from prosecution</strong></p><p style="text-align: justify;">Withdrawal from prosecution is subject to consent by the trial Judge and when the accused persons are still absconding the distraction ought not to have been exercised.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"><strong><em>Sreemati Prativa Raid Dey(Tirtha) Vs Dr. Mohammad Yousuf, Medical Officer, Emergency Department, Chittagong Medical College Hospital and others, 20BLD (AD) 54</em></strong></p><p style="text-align: justify;"><strong>Ref:</strong> 25 DLR 174; 35DLR(AD) 329, 30 DLR (AD)228; 31DLR (AD)134—Cited.</p><p><span id="pastemarkerend"> </span></p></div></div>
1054	<h2 class="blog_entry-title">CODE OF CRIMINAL PROCEDURE, 1898 [SECTION 496 - 561A]</h2>
<div class="entry-content"><div class="entry-content"><p><b>Citation:</b>  18BLD (HCD)680, 20BLD(AD)289,  19BLD(HCD)137,13BLD(HCD)367, 13 BLD(AD)190, 14BLD(AD) 220, 13BLD(HCD)492, 13 BLD(HCD)652, 18BLD(HCD)357, 13BLD(HCD)118, 13BLD(HCD)123, 13BLD(HCD)126,13BLD(HCD)224,18BLD(HCD)433,15BLD(AD)14, 15BLD(HCD)376,17BLD (AD) 163, 17B</p><p><b>Subject:</b>   CRIMINAL PROCEDURE</p><p><b>Delivery Date:</b>  1970-01-01</p><!DOCTYPE html><p> </p><p> </p><p align="center" style="text-align: center;"><strong> </strong></p><p align="center" style="text-align: center;"><strong>CODE OF CRIMINAL PROCEDURE, 1898</strong></p><p align="center" style="text-align: center;"><strong> </strong></p><p style="text-align: justify;"><strong>Sections—496, 497 and 498</strong></p><p style="text-align: justify;"><strong>Anticipatory Bail</strong></p><p style="text-align: justify;">A person apprehensive of arrest by a police officer or a Court may be admitted to bail either by the High Court Division or the Court of Sessions, but the power must be derivable from the express terms of section 496 or 497 of the Code. There is no inherent power of the High Court Division or the court of Sessions to grant bail at any stage. Therefore status in life, affluence or otherwise are irrelevant while considering the prayer for granting anticipatory bail.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"><strong><em>K. M. Jahangir Alam Vs The State, 18BLD (HCD)680</em></strong></p><p style="text-align: justify;"><strong> </strong></p><p style="text-align: justify;"><strong>Sections—496, 497 and 498</strong></p><p style="text-align: justify;"><strong>Anticipatory Bail</strong></p><p style="text-align: justify;">Section 498 like sections 497 does not require a person to place himself in custodian lagis, to be dealt with in accordance with law. Therefore, if he is allowed anticipatory bail then upon furnishing bond he will subject himself really to one form of custody. If the prayer is rejected or adinterim bail is allowed, but is subsequently cancelled, then the matter ends there and does not entail the consequence that he has to given into the police or jail custody. His position cannot be worse than before the refusal of his prayer for br cancellation of anticipatory bail.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"><strong><em>K. M. Jahangir Alam Vs The State, 18BLD (HCD)680</em></strong></p><p style="text-align: justify;"><strong>Ref:</strong> 10 C.W.N.1093 4 Cr1. L. J. 221; 721. A. 120; 19DLR(SC)38; 15BLD( 1995) (AD) 14—Referred</p><p style="text-align: justify;"><strong> </strong></p><p style="text-align: justify;"><strong>Sections—497/498</strong></p><p style="text-align: justify;"><strong>Constitution of Bangladesh, 1972</strong></p><p style="text-align: justify;"><strong>Articles—32 and 33</strong></p><p style="text-align: justify;">Section 497 of the Code speaks that when there is a reasonable ground for believing that a person is guilty of offence punishable with death or imprisonment for life, he should not be granted bail. Section 497 of the Code is a procedural law and the accused having alleged to have committed a substantive offence of murder his liberty is curtailed and as such the argument with regard to violation of fundamental right cannot be accepted in the facts of the instant case as law permits of such arrest and detention in custody.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"><strong><em>The State Vs Faisal Alam Ansari, 20BLD(AD)289</em></strong></p><p style="text-align: justify;"><strong> </strong></p><p style="text-align: justify;"><strong>Section—497(1)</strong></p><p style="text-align: justify;">Under sub-section (1) of section 497 of the Code an accused may not be released on bail if there appears reasonable grounds for believing that he has been guilty of an offence punishable with death or imprisonment for life. The proviso to the sub-section contain exceptions to cases of a person being under the age of sixteen years or a woman or any sick person.</p><p style="text-align: justify;">Reading the statement of co-accused Taheruddin Thakur recorded under section 164 of the Code and the statement of some of the witnesses recorded under section 161 of the Code it appears that there appears reasonable grounds for believing that they may be a party to a criminal conspiracy as alleged by the prosecution and as such the prayer for bail is rejected with a direction the State to take all necessary steps for medical care and attention of the petitioners, who are aged and said to be suffering from various ailments.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"><strong><em>K.M. Obaidur Rahman Vs The State, 19BLD(HCD)137</em></strong></p><p style="margin-bottom: 12.0pt;"><strong>Ref:</strong> Khaled Saigol Vs. The State, 14 DLR (SC)32 1—Cited</p><p style="margin-bottom: 12.0pt;"><strong> </strong></p><p style="margin-bottom: 12.0pt;"><strong>Section—497(1)</strong></p><p style="text-align: justify;">An accused who is not under the age of 16 years or any woman or any sick or infirm person can not be released on bail if there appear reasonable ground for believing that he has been guilty of an offence punishable with death or imprisonment for life. The fact that the accused has become a member of the Parliament is no ground at all for releasing him on bail since his case does not come within the purview of proviso to section 497(1) Cr.P.C.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"><strong><em>The State Vs. Auranga @ K. M. Hemayetuddin,13BLD(HCD)367</em></strong></p><p style="text-align: justify;"><strong>Ref:</strong> Nobin Vs. Russick, ILR 10 Cal. 268; Abdul Motaleb and others Vs. The State, 27 DLR 665—Cited</p><p style="text-align: justify;"><strong> </strong></p><p style="text-align: justify;"><strong>Section—497(l)</strong></p><p style="text-align: justify;">The prohibition under the section is that a person accused of any non-bailable offence shall not be released on bail if there appear reasonable grounds for believing that he has been guilty of an offence punishable with death or imprisonment for life.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"><strong><em>Shaikh Shahidul Islam Vs. The State, 13 BLD(AD)190</em></strong></p><p style="text-align: justify;"><strong> </strong></p><p style="text-align: justify;"><strong>Sections—497(1) and 498</strong></p><p style="text-align: justify;"><strong>Anticipatory Bail</strong></p><p style="text-align: justify;">Observations/findings made in an order while granting bail are made with an eye on section 497(1) Cr.P.C. for the purpose of bail only and these do not affect the merit of the case. Under special circumstances anticipatory bail may be granted even after submission of charge sheet.</p><p> </p><p> </p><p style="text-align: justify;"><strong><em>The State Vs. MA. Malik, 14BLD(AD) 220</em></strong></p><p style="text-align: justify;"><strong>Section—498</strong></p><p style="text-align: justify;">Order for conditional bail is illegal and not proper.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"><strong><em>AJI.M. Siddique Vs. The State, 13BLD (AD)1</em></strong></p><p style="text-align: justify;"><strong>Ref:</strong> 15DLR(SC)429:Crl. Appeal No. 9-D of 1 969(Unreported)—Cited</p><p style="text-align: justify;"><strong> </strong></p><p style="text-align: justify;"><strong>Section—498</strong></p><p style="text-align: justify;">Whether prayer for bail should be allowed in a case in which there are good grounds for success of the appeal along with other grounds. Held: In a case in which the accused is aged and respectable person and there are good grounds in the appeal arising out of conviction and sentence of 5 years R.I. and that there is no immediate prospect of getting the appeal heard, the prayer for bail should be allowed.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"><strong><em>Mizanur Rahman alias Majnu and another Vs. The State, 13BLD(HCD)492</em></strong></p><p style="text-align: justify;"><strong> </strong></p><p style="text-align: justify;"><strong>Section—498</strong></p><p style="text-align: justify;">In matters which are at the discretion of the Court, but which discretion need be exercised judicially, but not arbitrarily, it is to be seen whether there is any process issued by the Court in view of a case pending against the petitioner and there is an apprehension of not being given a fair hearing by local judicial authority, they having been allegedly influenced by the person in power.</p><p style="margin-bottom: 12.0pt;"><strong><em>Syed Wahidul Alam Vs The State, 13 BLD(HCD)652</em></strong></p><p style="margin-bottom: 12.0pt;"><strong> </strong></p><p style="margin-bottom: 12.0pt;"><strong>Section—498</strong></p><p style="text-align: justify;">In a sensational case involving brutal murder where the punishment is either death or imprisonment for life and there is a possibility that the accused may abscond and tamper with the evidence, the accused cannot be enlarged on bail to obstruct the course of justice.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"><strong><em>Major (Retd.) M. Khairuzzaman Vs. The State, 18BLD(HCD)357</em></strong></p><p style="text-align: justify;"><strong> </strong></p><p style="text-align: justify;"><strong>Section—498</strong></p><p style="text-align: justify;"><strong>Bail</strong></p><p style="text-align: justify;">Bail in non-bailable offence is a matter of discretion of the Court which has to be exercised with due care and caution and the facts and circumstances of the case—For an offence punishable with death or transportation for life, an accused charged with the same not to be released on bail if there are reasonable grounds for believing that the accused committed such an offence—Court to examine the data available in the case to find out whether reasonable grounds exist to connect the accused person with the crime alleged against him—Court’s belief on the point has to rest on the accusations made in the report to the police, the nature and credentials of the eveidence, which the prosecution proposes to lead in the case and all other relevant circum-stances surrounding the circumstances—Onus lies on the prosecution to disclose those reasonable grounds and the Court has to examine the data available in the case—No legal or moral compulsion to keep people in jail merely on the allegation of commission of offences punishable with death or transportation— Ultimate conviction and incarceration of a mate conviction and incarceration of a guilty person can repair the wrong caused by mistaken relief of interim bail granted to him but no satisfactory reparation can be offered to an innocent man for his unjustified incarceration at any stage of the case albeit his acquittal in the long run—58 persons who stand on the same footing having been enlarged on bail the same privilige granted to the petitions.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"><strong><em>Major(Rtd.) Md Matiur Rahrnan Vs The State 13BLD(HCD)118</em></strong></p><p style="text-align: justify;"><strong>Ref:</strong> PLD1972 S.C.81; 35 DLR (AD) 279—Cited</p><p style="text-align: justify;"><strong> </strong></p><p style="text-align: justify;"><strong>Section—498</strong></p><p style="text-align: justify;">Long delay in holding the trial, Court found reasonable to allow the petitioners to be released on bail till the commencement of trial.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"><strong><em>Major (Rtd.) Md.Matiur Rahman Vs. The State, 13BLD(HCD)123</em></strong></p><p style="text-align: justify;"><strong>Ref:</strong> PLD 1972 S.C.81 (84); (1988)8 BLD (AD)21—Cited</p><p style="text-align: justify;"><strong> </strong></p><p style="text-align: justify;"><strong>Section—498</strong></p><p style="text-align: justify;">90 persons named in F.I.R—60 persons arrested—out of 60 persons 58 persons released on bail by courts below—petitioners arrested</p><p style="text-align: justify;">13.12.89—Police submitted charge-sheet on 18.1.91 petitioners involved in the case for colateral purposes in order to harass and humiliate the accused petitioners before the public—petitioners stand on the same equal footing—more than a year elepased since the submission of charge-sheet—not known when the trial will commence—petitioners prayer for bail deserve consideration.</p><p style="margin-bottom: 12.0pt;"><strong><em>Major (Red.) Md. Matiur Rahman and another Vs. The State, 13BLD(HCD)126</em></strong></p><p style="margin-bottom: 12.0pt;"><strong> </strong></p><p style="margin-bottom: 12.0pt;"><strong>Complaint Case</strong></p><p style="text-align: justify;"><strong>Appearance of the accused in a complaint case</strong></p><p style="text-align: justify;">In a complaint case, on the first date fixed for appearance of the accused as well as on each subsequent date to which the hearing may be adjourned, the complainant (if he is not a public servant) must personally appear before the Court and that in case of the failure of the complainant to appear in the Court on any such date, it is imperative for the Magistrate to acquit the summoned accused persons unless for some reasons the Magistrate thinks it proper to adjourn the hearing of the case to some other date.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"><strong><em>Md. Ayub Ali Bangali Vs. Mia Munir Ahmed, 13BLD(HCD)224</em></strong>.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"><strong>Ref:</strong> A.I.R. 1948 (Madras) 45; 36 DLR. 349—Cited</p><p style="text-align: justify;"><strong> </strong></p><p style="text-align: justify;"><strong>Section—498</strong></p><p style="text-align: justify;"><strong>Ad-interim Bail</strong></p><p style="text-align: justify;">When an accused is enlarged on ad-interim bail granted by the High Court Division during the pendency of the Rule, a Court subordinate to the High Court Division has no authority to cancel the said ad-interim bail. Such a Court may bring the misuse of privilege of such bail to the notice of the High Court Division which is in seisin of the matter till disposal of the Rule. If such misuse of the privilege of the bail is brought to the notice of the High Court Division during pendency of the Rule, the High Court Division would certainly take into consideration such fact in disposing of the Rule. Only after disposal of a Rule confirming the adinterim bail by the High Court Division a subordinate Court would be competent to cancel the bail for misusing the privilege of such bail.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"><strong><em>Dr. Mominur Rahman alias Zinna and another Vs The State, 18BLD(HCD)433</em></strong></p><p style="text-align: justify;"><strong>Ref:</strong> 18BLD(HCD)(1998)172—Cited</p><p style="text-align: justify;"><strong> </strong></p><p style="text-align: justify;"><strong>Section—498</strong></p><p style="text-align: justify;"><strong>Anticipatory Bail</strong></p><p style="text-align: justify;">Section 498 Cr.P.C. gives extended and wider powers to the High Court Division for granting bail in non-bailable offences but this power must be exercised in a reasonable and judicial manner so that the normal practice founded on justice and equity is not disregarded, barring exceptional circumstances.</p><p style="text-align: justify;">Considering the facts that the two co-accused persons were earlier refused bail by the learned Magistrate and the offending article, being on print, is not likely to be tampered with and there being little chance of the appellant’s jumping the bail, the Appellate Division allowed bail to the petitioner.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"><strong><em>Md. Atiqullah Khan Masud Vs The State and another, 15BLD(AD)14</em></strong></p><p style="text-align: justify;"><strong>Ref:</strong> 19DLR (SC)38 (54): PLD 1966 (SC) 1003 (1022-1023);—Cited</p><p style="text-align: justify;"><strong> </strong></p><p style="text-align: justify;"><strong>Section—498</strong></p><p style="text-align: justify;">The chargesheet having contained no allegation of any specific overt act against the accused-petitioners, they being in custody for a pretty long time, co-accused being on bail and there being no prospect of an early trial and the petitioners being fairly advanced in age are considered mitigating circumstances for allowing bail to them.</p><p style="margin-bottom: 12.0pt;"><strong><em>Sultan Ahmed and another Vs. The State, 15BLD(HCD)376</em></strong></p><p style="margin-bottom: 12.0pt;"><strong> </strong></p><p style="margin-bottom: 12.0pt;"><strong>Section—498</strong></p><p style="text-align: justify;"><strong>Bail</strong></p><p style="text-align: justify;">There is nothing on record except the alleged statement of a co-accused that the real planning for the occurrence was done by the respondent. Even the alleged confession belies the alleged incriminating statement. The materials on record are plainly insufficient to think that there are reasonable grounds for believing that the respondent has been guilty of the alleged criminal conspiracy.</p><p style="text-align: justify;">Law permits granting of bail even in a case where there are even reasonable grounds for refusing bail in the case of any women or any sick or infirm person. The respondent has not been granted bail upon these considerations but upon the view that there are no reasonable grounds for believing that she has been guilty of the offence alleged and the said view suffers from no legal infirmity.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"><strong><em>The State Vs Jobaida Rashid, 17BLD (AD) 163</em></strong></p><p style="text-align: justify;"><strong> </strong></p><p style="text-align: justify;"><strong>Section—498</strong></p><p style="text-align: justify;">Gravity of the offence by itself is not a ground for refusing bail when the prosecution fails to produce any material before the Court to connect the accused petitioner with the alleged offence.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"><strong><em>Abdul Kader Faruque alias Mohd. Faruque Vs The State, 17BLD(HCD)148</em></strong></p><p style="text-align: justify;"><strong> </strong></p><p style="text-align: justify;"><strong>Section—498</strong></p><p style="text-align: justify;">From a perusal of F.LR., chargesheet, age certificate and other papers it appears that several accused persons threw stones including petitioner No. I but in the postmortem report there is a reference to seven injuries. Moreover the postmortem report does not show any injury on the chest of the victim. From the certificate issued by the Head Master of the school it shows that at the time of occurrence the petitioner No. I was merely 14 years old. The petitioner voluntarily surrendered before the trial Court and out of ten accuseds eight have already been enlarged on bail. In the circumstances this Court held that ends of justice will be met if the petitioner is enlarged on bail.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"><strong><em>Asik Miah and another Vs The State, 17BLD(HCD)253</em></strong></p><p style="text-align: justify;"><strong> </strong></p><p style="text-align: justify;"><strong>Section—498</strong></p><p style="text-align: justify;"><strong>Delay in holding trial provides ground for bail</strong></p><p style="text-align: justify;">In this case the learned Magistrate ordered for further investigation of the case by the police and it is not known when such investigation will be completed and the case sent to the appropriate Court for trial. Trial of the case is likely to be delayed for unlimited period. In the circumstances, a case for bail is made out.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"><strong><em>Shahed Reza Shamim Vs The State, 17BLD (HCD)310</em></strong></p><p style="text-align: justify;"><strong> </strong></p><p style="text-align: justify;"><strong>Section—498</strong></p><p style="text-align: justify;"><strong>Bail</strong></p><p style="text-align: justify;">Mere naming the petitioner in the charge-sheet without any prima facie material and the mere fact that in the occurrence the Head of the State with his family has been murdered and that this is a sensational case cannot be grounds for refusal of bail.</p><p style="margin-bottom: 12.0pt;"><strong><em>Jobaida Rashid Vs The State, 17BLD (HCD)366</em></strong></p><p style="margin-bottom: 12.0pt;"><strong>Ref:</strong> 27 DLR (AD) 29; 37DLR (AD) 139; 7 BCR (AD) 143—Cited</p><p style="text-align: justify;"><strong> </strong></p><p style="text-align: justify;"><strong>Section—498</strong></p><p style="text-align: justify;"><strong>Power of granting anticipatory bail</strong></p><p style="text-align: justify;">Power of granting anticipatory bail is very sparingly used by the High Court Division to save a citizen from unnecessary harassment and humiliation in the hand of police on flimsy grounds or with ulterior motive or out of political designs. This power cannot be exercised in each and every case as a substitute to the exercise of such power by the court below. A person cannot be enlarged on anticipatory bail how high so ever he may be unless conditions for granting such bail are satisfied.</p><p style="text-align: justify;">In the instant case the petitioner has not been able to make out a case of unnecessary harassment and humiliation in the hands of police and as such he is not entitled to anticipatory bail.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"><strong><em>Md. Belayet Hossain Sharif Vs. The State, 18BLD(HCD)172</em></strong></p><p style="text-align: justify;"><strong> </strong></p><p style="text-align: justify;"><strong>Anticipatory bail</strong></p><p style="text-align: justify;">From the F.I.R. it appears that there is no mention of specific allegation against the petitioner, simply his name has been mentioned as former Director of the Company, that there is no ingredients of offence against the petitioner. If he is compelled to go to the court below he may be unnecessarily harassed, Moreover, when the matter has come before the High Court Division and it is in seisin of the matter. It cannot shut its eyes and push him to uncertainty in another forum and as such he should be granted him bail. <strong><em>[per Muhammad Abdul Mannan, J.] </em></strong></p><p style="text-align: justify;"><strong><em>Md. Belayet Hossain Sharif Vs. The State, 18BLD(HCD)172</em></strong></p><p style="text-align: justify;"><strong> </strong></p><p style="text-align: justify;"><strong>Anticipatory bail</strong></p><p style="text-align: justify;">A Court of law does not make any distinction between the rich and the poor, the high and the law. A man with a high social standing ranks equal before a Court of law with a man sleeping rough on the pavement in front of the Curzon Hall. No one is entitled to claim a privilege for himself nor can he claim preferential treatment in a Court of law on account of his wealth or status. So, innocence simpliciter is not a ground for anticipatory bail. However high one may be one must have respect for the Courts and should not hesitate to appear before a Magistrate on the ground of one’s standing in the society. <strong><em>[per Syed Amirul Islam, J]</em></strong></p><p style="text-align: justify;"><strong><em>Md. Belayet Hossain Sharif Vs. The State, 18BLD(HCD)1 72</em></strong></p><p style="text-align: justify;"><strong>Ref:</strong> 5DLR(FC) 143; 1 5DLR(SC)2; 18 DLR (SC)393; 19DLR(SC)38; PLD1974 (Lahore)256; 12BLD440; 12BLD3 14;2BLT(HCD) 164;5BLD(AD)1 10; 14BLD(AD)222; 14BLD (AD)14—Cited</p><p style="text-align: justify;"><strong> </strong></p><p style="text-align: justify;"><strong>Section—498</strong></p><p style="text-align: justify;"><strong>Anticipatory Bail</strong></p><p style="text-align: justify;">On going through the application filed by the petitioner and also after hearing the learned Advocate this Court is not satisfied as to the cause of his non-appearance before the Magistrate. Moreover the offence with which the petitioner has been charged punishable with death or imprisonment for life anticipatory bail cannot be granted though the petitioner is an elected Chairman.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"><strong><em>Abdur Rahman Molla Vs. The State, 18BLD(HCD)247</em></strong></p><p style="text-align: justify;"><strong>Ref:</strong> 18BLD172; 15DLR(SC)2; 15BLD (AD) 14—Cited</p><p style="text-align: justify;"><strong> </strong></p><p style="text-align: justify;"><strong>Section—498</strong></p><p style="text-align: justify;">There are sufficient reasonable grounds appearing for believing that the accused-petitioner as an architect had direct complicity in the commission of the offence of the triple murder and hence the High Court Division held that the accused-petitioner is not entitled to get any bail in the instant case.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"><strong><em>Shaik Mohammad Aslam alias Md. Aslam alias Sweeden Aslam Vs The State, 18BLD (HCD)649</em></strong></p><p style="text-align: justify;"><strong>Ref:</strong> 23DLR(SC)41; 35 DLR (AD)279; 7 BCR(AD) 143—Cited.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"><strong> </strong></p><p style="text-align: justify;"><strong>Section—498</strong></p><p style="text-align: justify;">The provision for bail in a criminal case beginning from the initiation of a proceeding upto the conclusion of the trial has been made in Chapter XXXIX of the Code of Cfiminal Procedure. It is well-settled that the basic conception of the word ‘bail’ is release of a person from the custody of police and delivery into the hands of sureties, who undertake to produce him in Court whenever required to do so. An accused person is said, at common law, to be admitted to bail, when he is released from the custody of the officers of the Court and is entrusted to the custody of persons known as his sureties who are bound to produce him to answer, at a specified time and place, the charge against him and who in default of so doing are liable to forfeit such sum as is specified when bail is granted. <strong><em>[Per A.T.M. Afzal, CJ]</em></strong></p><p style="text-align: justify;"><strong><em>The State Vs Abdul Wahab Shah Chowdhury, 19BLD(AD)189</em></strong></p><p style="text-align: justify;"><strong> </strong></p><p style="text-align: justify;"><strong>Section—498</strong></p><p style="text-align: justify;"><strong>Pre-arrest or anticipatory bail</strong></p><p style="text-align: justify;">There is no dispute that the prayer for pre-arrest or anticipatory bail can be made only under section 498 of the Code and under no other section of the Code. The High Court Division and the Court of Sessions have concurrent power under the section.</p><p style="text-align: justify;">The pre-arrest or anticipatory bail is an extraordinary remedy, and an exception to the general law of bail which can be granted only in extraordinary and exceptional circumstances upon a proper and intelligent exercise of discretion. The ordinary law is that a person accused of a non-bailable offence must appear before the Court taking cognizance for making a prayer for bail. The prayer can be made when he is arrested or detained with or without warrant and is brought before the said Court. Pre-arrest bail is an exception to the general law and the Court will always bear in mind the caution of. <strong>[Per A.T.M. Afzal, CJ.]</strong></p><p style="text-align: justify;"><strong><em>The State Vs Abdul Wahab Shah Chowdhury, 19BLD(AD)189</em></strong></p><p style="text-align: justify;"><strong> </strong></p><p style="text-align: justify;"><strong>Anticipatory Bail—Public Commotion</strong></p><p style="text-align: justify;">The prayer may also be considered may occur if it is proved that on account of some local public commotion or other circumstances it is not possible for the petitioner to appear before the lower Court for seeking bail. The petitioner must, however, remain physically present in Court before his application for bail can be entertained. The Court, if it grants anticipatory bail, must expressly make it a condition that if the petitioner commits any breach of the terms of bail, the Court concerned will be at liberty to cancel his bail and take him into custody. <strong>[Per A.T.M. Afzal, CJ.]</strong></p><p style="text-align: justify;"><strong><em>The State Vs Abdul Wahab Shah Chowdhury, 19BLD(AD)189</em></strong></p><p style="text-align: justify;"><strong> </strong></p><p style="text-align: justify;"><strong>Anticipatory Bail</strong></p><p style="text-align: justify;">Anticipatory bail should be granted by the High Court Division for a limited period or till filing of the charge-sheet, whichever is appropriate in the circumstances of the case. After expiry of the period or filing of the chare-sheet, as the case may be, the accused must appear before the Court concerned and obtain fresh bail from the Court on the merit of the case.<strong>(Per Latifur Rahman,J)</strong></p><p style="text-align: justify;"><strong><em>The State Vs Abdul Wahab Shah Chowdhury, 19BLD(AD)189</em></strong></p><p style="text-align: justify;"><strong> </strong></p><p style="text-align: justify;"><strong>Anticipatory Bail</strong></p><p style="text-align: justify;">The Court, if it grants anticipatory bail, must expressly make it a condition that if the petitioner commits any breach of the terms of bail, the Court concerned will be at liberty to cancel his bail and take him into custody.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"><strong>[Per A.T.M. Afzal, CJ)</strong></p><p style="text-align: justify;"><strong><em>The State Vs Abdul Wahab Shah Chowdhury, 19BLD(AD)189</em></strong></p><p style="text-align: justify;"><strong> </strong></p><p style="text-align: justify;"><strong>Sections—497 and 498</strong></p><p style="text-align: justify;">Ordinarily when a person is wanted in connection with a non-bailable offence of grave nature he is not entitled to anticipatory bail. All persons charged with non-bailable offences must be treated equally unless, of course, there are special circumstances which need special consideration in a particular facts of a case.</p><p style="text-align: justify;">Granting of anticipatory bail is an extraordinary remedy and as such in the case of accusations of non-bailable offences anticipatory bail should not be granted and the person should be directed to seek bail under section 497 of the Code. <strong>[Per Latifur Rahnian, J.]</strong></p><p style="text-align: justify;"><strong><em>The State Vs Abdul Wahab Shah Chowdhury, 19BLD(AD)189</em></strong></p><p style="text-align: justify;"><strong> </strong></p><p style="text-align: justify;"><strong>Section—498</strong></p><p style="text-align: justify;">Anticipatory bail lost its force after submission of charge sheet and taking of cognizance by the Court concerned. The accused cannot claim to continue on the anticipatory bail even after submission of the charge sheet and taking of cognizance of offence by the Court concerned.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"><strong><em>Probir Kumar Chowdhury alias Tinku and others Vs The State, 19BLD(HCD)4</em></strong></p><p style="text-align: justify;"><strong> </strong></p><p style="text-align: justify;"><strong>Section—498</strong></p><p style="text-align: justify;"><strong>Anticipatory bail</strong></p><p style="text-align: justify;">Power of granting anticipatory bail is very sparingly used by this Court to save a citizen from unnecessary harassment and humiliation in the hand of police on flimsy ground or with ulterior motive or out of political designs. This power cannot be exercised in each and every case as a substitute in the exercise of such power by the court below. A person cannot be enlarged on anticipatory bail how high so ever he may be unless conditions for granting such bail are satisfied.</p><p style="margin-bottom: 12.0pt;"><strong><em>Nurul Islam and others Vs. The State, 19BLD(HCD)173</em></strong></p><p style="margin-bottom: 12.0pt;"><strong>Ref:</strong> 18 BLD(1998) (HCD)172—relied upon. 5BLD (1985)(AD)1l0; 46 DLR315; 48 DLR 18 ;47DLR33; 43DLR3 12—Not applicable.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"><strong> </strong></p><p style="text-align: justify;"><strong>Section—500</strong></p><p style="text-align: justify;"><strong>Discharge from custody</strong></p><p style="text-align: justify;">The term ‘discharge” has not been defined in the Code of Criminal Procedure but nevertheless the word “discharge” connotes different meanings in different contexts. When an accused is discharged pursuant to a final report by the police, it means that the accused has been discharged from custody under section 500 of the Code and not discharged from the case. In such a case a second prosecution is permissible in law as the order of discharge was not passed on merit.</p><p style="text-align: justify;">If cognizance is taken on the basis of a fresh complaint or a naraji petition, which also amounts to a fresh complaint, there can be no objection to the proceedings at all. In an appropriate case an application for revival of the case against the discharged accused may also amount to a fresh complaint. A Magistrate is competent to take cognizance on the basis of a naraji petition or a fresh complaint by complying with the requirements of the Code.</p><p style="text-align: justify;">In the instant case the order of discharge of the accused petitioner from custody on the recommendation of police did not render the Magistrate functus officio and it cannot operate as a bar in taking cognizance against the discharged accused by the Magistrate concerned.</p><p style="margin-bottom: 12.0pt;"><strong><em>Nurul Hoque Vs. Bazal Ahmed and 3 others, 15BLD(HCD)231</em></strong></p><p style="text-align: justify;"><strong>Ref:</strong> 30DLR344; 29DLR(SC)256—Cited</p><p style="text-align: justify;"><strong> </strong></p><p style="text-align: justify;"><strong>Section—504</strong></p><p style="text-align: justify;">The expression property occurring in section 504 of the Criminal Procedure Code, whether should be given a narrow construction.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"><strong><em>A.K.M. Siddique Vs. The State, 13BLD (HCD)85</em></strong></p><p style="text-align: justify;"><strong> </strong></p><p style="text-align: justify;"><strong>Section—509A</strong></p><p style="text-align: justify;">Mere filing of an application by the Public Prosecutor informing the court that the doctor concerned is away from the country cannot be the permissible substitute for legal evidence as it does not fulfill any of the conditions laid down in section 509A.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"><strong><em>Ataur Rahman and others Vs. The State, 14BLD(HCD)391</em></strong></p><p style="text-align: justify;"><strong> </strong></p><p style="text-align: justify;"><strong>Section—517</strong></p><p style="text-align: justify;">Under the provisions of section 517 of the Code a Special Tribunal may pass necessary order for disposal of a property seized during investigation after the disposal of the case.</p><p style="text-align: justify;">After the discharge of the accused on submission of final report duly accepted by the court, it cannot be said that the property seized has been used in connection with any offence and as such the said property cannot be confiscated and it must be returned to the persons from whose possession it was seized.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"><strong><em>S.A. Hasnat Khan and others Vs. The State, 15BLD(HCD)440</em></strong></p><p style="text-align: justify;"><strong> </strong></p><p style="text-align: justify;"><strong>Section—517(1)</strong></p><p style="text-align: justify;">For an order to be passed under the aforesaid provision for disposal of the goods after the conclusion of an enquiry or trial, the Court has to satisfy itself as to the conditions mentioned therein, one of the conditions is that the goods must be produced before it or in its custody.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"><strong><em>Sompong Vs The State, 13BLD(AD)121</em></strong></p><p style="text-align: justify;"><strong> </strong></p><p style="text-align: justify;"><strong>Section—522(1)</strong></p><p style="text-align: justify;"><strong>Power to restore possession of immovable property</strong></p><p style="text-align: justify;">It provides that whenever a person is convicted of an offence attended by criminal force or show of force or by criminal intimidation and it appears to the court that by such force or show of force or criminal intimidation any person has been dispossessed of any immovable property, the court may, if it thinks fit, when convicting such person or at any time within one month from the date or the conviction order the person dispossessed to be restored to the possession of the same.</p><p style="text-align: justify;">In the instant case the use of force, show of force or criminal intimidation at the time of criminal trespass upon the case land had not been held proved in the trial court or in the appellate court. The High Court Division has found no illegality in the said concurrent findings. In the circumstances the said Court has acted beyond jurisdiction in passing the order for restoration of possession of case land to the complainant.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"><strong><em>Mohammad Ali Member Vs Abdul Fazul Mia Md. Mazedul Huq and another, 19BLD (AD)260</em></strong></p><p style="text-align: justify;"><strong> </strong></p><p style="text-align: justify;"><strong>Section—526</strong></p><p style="text-align: justify;">There is an apprehension in the mind of the accused-petitioners in the matter of getting fair and impartial trial in the hands of any Sessions Judge under the Sessions Division, Dhaka and also since they lost confidence, the case is required to be transferred from the Sessions Division, Dhaka to any other Sessions Judge of any other Sessions Division around Dhaka. The Sessions Division of Narsingdi is around Dhaka and it will be convenient for both the parties if the case is transferred to the said Session Division and trial is concluded there.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"><strong><em>Sohali Thakur and ors Vs. The State, 19BLD(HCD)103</em></strong></p><p style="text-align: justify;"><strong><em>[The case has been reversed by Appellate Division, reported in 20BLD(AD)(2000)85]</em></strong></p><p style="text-align: justify;"><strong>Ref:</strong> Serjeant Vs. Dale (1877) 2 Queen Bench Division and Rex Vs. Sussex Justices (1924)1 PLD 1 973(SC) 327—Cited.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"><strong> </strong></p><p style="text-align: justify;"><strong>Section—526</strong></p><p style="text-align: justify;">Under this section the High Court Division may on its own motion transfer a criminal case pending before any subordinate court without issuing any notice upon the contesting parties but such transfer is to be made only when it tends to the general convenience of the parties or the witnesses and it is expedient for the ends of justice. The High Court Division may also withdraw a case to itself without issuing any notice upon either parties when it is found that some question of law of unusual difficulty is involved in the case. In the instant case, neither of these conditions being present the impugned order of transfer of the case is set aside.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"><strong><em>Md. Sirajul islam alias Siraj Madbar and others Vs. Keramat Ali Bhuiyan and another, 15BLD(AD)1</em></strong></p><p style="text-align: justify;"><strong> </strong></p><p style="text-align: justify;"><strong>Section—526</strong></p><p style="text-align: justify;">The High Court Division can suo motu transfer a sessions case. The informant and his victim brother by preferring the application has merely informed the High Court Division about the state of the circumstances surrounding the concerned sessions case and the High Court Division had complete jurisdiction to exercise its discretion in the matter.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"><strong><em>Jahir Gazi and others Vs Belal Hossain, Advocate and others, 19BLD(AD)85</em></strong></p><p style="text-align: justify;"><strong> </strong></p><p style="text-align: justify;"><strong>Section—526</strong></p><p style="text-align: justify;">Mere fact of taking into custody of the accused during trial can never be a basis for making a prayer for transfer of the case unless there is other convincing and reasonable grounds for apprehension in the mind of the accused.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"><strong><em>Md. Nurul Alam Vs Sohail Thakur &amp; ors., 20BLD(AD)85</em></strong></p><p style="text-align: justify;"><strong> </strong></p><p style="text-align: justify;"><strong>Section—526 (1)</strong></p><p style="text-align: justify;"><strong>Transfer of a Criminal Case</strong></p><p style="text-align: justify;">In determining the venue of trial of a criminal case in a transfer petition, the general conveniences of the contending parties is to be taken into consideration. Since the central point in dispute in the 4 criminal cases in question relates to three transactions by cheques and dishonour of those cheques and non-supply of jute against payment and one of those cases being criminal case No.C-144 of 1993 having already been transferred to the court of the Magistrate at Dhaka, the reasons for not allowing the transfer of 3 other cases from Kotchandpur to Dhaka is not based on proper exercise of the discretion by the High Court Division. The 3 criminal cases are therefore transferred from the Court of the Thana Magistrate, Kotchandpur (Jhenaidah) to the Court of the Magistrate at Dhaka.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"><strong><em>M. M. Nurul Hoque Mollah Vs. Sree Radheshyam Saha and another, 15BLD (AD)33</em></strong></p><p><strong><em> </em></strong></p><p> </p><p style="text-align: justify;"><strong>Section—526</strong></p><p style="text-align: justify;">In an application under section 526 of the Code filed by the informant a Division Bench of the High Court transferred Sessions Case No. 83 of 1998 from the Court of Additional Sessions Judge to the Court of Sessions Judge, Nawabganj for trial. The said order was passed exparte without any notice either to the accused or to the State and without calling for any report from the Court concerned. The alleged ground of transfer were not even noticed in the impugned order but even then transfer was allowed by merely saying that “without accepting or rejecting the grounds for the transfer, we think justice will be met if the case is disposed of by the Court of Sessions Judge, Nawabganj”.</p><p style="text-align: justify;">Such kind of order is far from a judicial order. If that be the way of disposing an application for transfer by throwing all procedures and norms to the winds, then, arbitrary was said to be the concern of the learned will rule the field and not ‘justice’ which Judges for passing the impugned order. It seems the learned Judge has a pathological disposing for passing such summary order which is absolutely wrong.</p><p style="text-align: justify;"><strong><em>Mohd. Moslem Uddin Vs The State &amp; anr, 19BLD(AD)247</em></strong></p><p style="text-align: justify;"><strong> </strong></p><p style="text-align: justify;"><strong>Section—526(1)(c)</strong></p><p style="text-align: justify;">The petitioner alleged that he has been threatened by the other side in open Court to be picked up from the Court with no hope to return and there is also pressure on his lawyer not to defend him. It is difficult to assess the scale of threat to his life or its existence or non-existence.
